position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">While you are right that JavaScript is technically visible, "easy" is relative here. Reverse engineering JSLinux is difficult for several reasons:<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Code Obfuscation:</span>&nbsp;The public JavaScript files are heavily&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">minified and obfuscated</span>. This means variable names are shortened to single letters (e.g.,&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">a</code>,&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">b</code>,&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">c</code>), and formatting is stripped, making the logic flow hard to track.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Emulation Complexity:</span>&nbsp;Even with clean code, you are looking at a virtualized environment. The core CPU execution loop (the&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">exec</code>&nbsp;function) is a massive, complex block that handles thousands of lines of instruction decoding and ALU logic.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Machine-Generated JS:</span>&nbsp;Because modern versions are&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">compiled from C</span>, the resulting JavaScript or Wasm doesn't look like code a human would write. It resembles assembly more than a high-level scripting language.</span><span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 86.9141px;"><img src="https://encrypted-tbn0.gstatic.com/faviconV2?url=https://bellard.org&amp;client=AIM&amp;size=128&amp;type=FAVICON&amp;fallback_opts=TYPE,SIZE,URL" alt="Bellard.org" style="background: rgb(255, 255, 255); border-radius: 20px; height: 12px; margin-right: 4px; width: 12px; flex-shrink: 0;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">Bellard.org</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+4</span></span></div></span></span></li></ul><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Fun Fact:</span>&nbsp;A few developers have actually tried to&nbsp;<span><a rel="noopener" href="https://github.com/jslinux/jslinux" style="text-decoration-thickness: 1px; text-decoration-color: var(--JKqx2); -webkit-tap-highlight-color: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.1); text-underline-offset: 1px; outline: 0px;">manually de-obfuscate</a></span>&nbsp;the 2011 version. They noted it was "therapeutic" but required intense effort to rename variables and document the clever tricks Bellard used, such as using XOR operations to simulate a Translation Lookaside Buffer (TLB).<span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 97.9766px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">Hacker News</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+2</span></span></div></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">Would you like to try&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">examining the source</span>&nbsp;of one of the older versions to see how it's structured?<span href="https://bellard.org/jslinux/tech.html#:~:text=History,js%20version." style="text-decoration-line: none; -webkit-tap-highlight-color: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.1); position: absolute; inset: 2px; -webkit-box; -webkit-box-orient: vertical; -webkit-line-clamp: 2; overflow: hidden; white-space-collapse: collapse;"><span>JSLinux - Technical Notes</span></div><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); margin: 0px 0px 8px; font-size: 12px; line-height: 1.3; display: -webkit-box; -webkit-box-orient: vertical; -webkit-line-clamp: 2; overflow: hidden; white-space-collapse: collapse;"><span>JSLinux - Technical Notes * History. This emulator has a long history. padding: 4px 20px 16px;"><div role="button" tabindex="0" style="align-items: stretch; border-radius: 9999px; color: var(--jINu6c); cursor: pointer; display: flex; justify-content: center; overflow: hidden; position: relative; background-color: var(--aYn2S); outline: 0px;"><span style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 20px; margin: 8px 16px;">Show all</span></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div></div><div></div></div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div></div></div></div><div style="--fade-in-animation: fade-in-new-response 150ms cubic-bezier(0.3,0,0.8,0.15); animation: var(--fade-in-animation); padding-top: 30px; position: relative; margin-top: 24px;"><div style="position: relative; padding-bottom: 10px; max-width: 652px; z-index: 1; margin-top: 0px;"><div><div style="display: flex; gap: 4px; margin-left: auto; width: fit-content;"><div style="display: flex; position: relative; overflow: hidden; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 24px 4px 24px 24px; padding: 12px 16px; width: fit-content; flex-direction: column; max-inline-size: 472px; margin-left: auto;"><div style="display: flex; flex-direction: row;"><span role="heading" style="-webkit-box-orient: vertical; -webkit-line-clamp: 2; display: -webkit-box; overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; overflow-wrap: break-word; font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 16px; line-height: 24px;">only 10k lines? how much is the coverage of jslinux?</span></div></div></div><div style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: flex; font-size: 12px; justify-content: end; line-height: 16px;"></div><div></div></div></div><div><div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div></div><div></div><div><div><div style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--m3c11,#eef0ff); position: relative; --m3c9: #e6e8f0; --m3c11: #e6e8f0; display: flex;"><div style="width: 652.438px;"><div><div style="display: contents;"></div></div><div dir="ltr" style="width: 652px; max-width: var(--CYi3c--fRcLaf,652px);"><div style="display: contents;"><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);"><div style="display: contents;">The original 2011 version of JSLinux is a masterclass in "minimalist yet functional" engineering. While 10,000 lines (actually closer to&nbsp;</div><span style="font-weight: 700;">7,000–8,000 lines</span>&nbsp;of formatted code) seems small for a PC emulator, its "coverage" is strategically focused to do exactly one thing: boot a modern OS.<span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 107.766px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">Stack Overflow</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+1</span></span></div></span></span></div><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">2011 Architecture Coverage<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">In its 2011 "Proof of Concept" state, JSLinux did not aim for 100% x86 compatibility. Instead, it targeted a specific subset required for the Linux kernel:<span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 109.852px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">WordPress.com</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+1</span></span></div></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">CPU Level:</span>&nbsp;Roughly equivalent to an&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">Intel 486</span>.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Instruction Set:</span>&nbsp;It supported basic 32-bit x86 instructions but lacked specialized extensions common today:</span><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: circle; padding-inline-start: 0px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">No FPU (Floating Point Unit):</span>&nbsp;It didn't need one because the Linux kernel has a built-in FPU emulator to handle math if the hardware lacks it.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: circle; padding-inline-start: 0px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">No Multimedia:</span>&nbsp;No MMX, SSE, or SSE2 support in the early version.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: circle; padding-inline-start: 0px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">No 16-bit Modes:</span>&nbsp;It skipped real mode and 16-bit protected mode, jumping straight to 32-bit execution.</span></li></ul></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Memory Management:</span>&nbsp;It included a&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">complete MMU</span>&nbsp;(Memory Management Unit) supporting paging, which is the "hard part" of running Linux.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Hardware Devices:</span>&nbsp;It emulated only the bare essentials:</span><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: circle; padding-inline-start: 0px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">8259 Programmable Interrupt Controller (PIC).</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: circle; padding-inline-start: 0px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">8254 Programmable Interrupt Timer (PIT).</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: circle; padding-inline-start: 0px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">16450 UART (for the serial console).</span><span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 86.3438px;"><img src="https://encrypted-tbn0.gstatic.com/faviconV2?url=https://bellard.org&amp;client=AIM&amp;size=128&amp;type=FAVICON&amp;fallback_opts=TYPE,SIZE,URL" alt="Bellard.org" style="background: rgb(255, 255, 255); border-radius: 20px; height: 12px; margin-right: 4px; width: 12px; flex-shrink: 0;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">Bellard.org</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+3</span></span></div></span></span></li></ul></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">Modern JSLinux Coverage (The "Wasm" Era)<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">The current version you see on&nbsp;<span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">Bellard's site</span>&nbsp;has vastly expanded coverage because it is based on&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">TinyEMU</span>:<span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 71.4219px;"><img src="https://encrypted-tbn0.gstatic.com/faviconV2?url=https://bellard.org&amp;client=AIM&amp;size=128&amp;type=FAVICON&amp;fallback_opts=TYPE,SIZE,URL" alt="Bellard.org" style="background: rgb(255, 255, 255); border-radius: 20px; height: 12px; margin-right: 4px; width: 12px; flex-shrink: 0;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">Bellard.org</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;"></span></span></div></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">CPU:</span>&nbsp;Full&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">64-bit x86</span>&nbsp;(and RISC-V) support.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Extensions:</span>&nbsp;Includes&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">AVX-512</span>,&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">SSE4.2</span>,&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">MMX</span>, and even&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">AMD-V (SVM)</span>&nbsp;virtualization extensions, allowing it to run QEMU&nbsp;<em style="font-weight: inherit;">inside</em>&nbsp;the browser.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Graphics:</span>&nbsp;Supports a simple framebuffer and the Fluxbox window manager.</span><span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 86.3438px;"><img src="https://encrypted-tbn0.gstatic.com/faviconV2?url=https://bellard.org&amp;client=AIM&amp;size=128&amp;type=FAVICON&amp;fallback_opts=TYPE,SIZE,URL" alt="Bellard.org" style="background: rgb(255, 255, 255); border-radius: 20px; height: 12px; margin-right: 4px; width: 12px; flex-shrink: 0;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">Bellard.org</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+3</span></span></div></span></span></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">Why so few lines?<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">The brevity comes from Bellard’s extreme efficiency and the fact that an emulator doesn't need to implement every possible hardware edge case—only the ones the Linux kernel actually probes during boot. By ignoring legacy 16-bit DOS compatibility and leveraging the kernel's own software-based math (FPU), he stripped the x86 architecture down to its core logic.<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">Do you want to see a specific breakdown of the&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">opcode decoding loop</span>&nbsp;from one of those de-obfuscated versions?<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div></div><div><div style="clear: both; display: align-items: center;"><div style="display: flex;"><div style="position: relative; display: inline-flex;"><span style="inline-size: 20px; block-size: 20px;"><div><svg fill="currentColor" width="20px" Even in its original 2011 release, Fabrice Bellard included a working C compiler within the emulated environment.<span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Standard Workflow</span>: You can write a C program using the included&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">qemacs</code>&nbsp;editors, then compile and run it directly in the terminal.</span><div style="margin-block: 24px 32px; </span></code></pre></div></div><div style="display: flex; justify-content: space-between; align-items: center; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px 4px 16px 16px; margin-top: 3px; overflow: hidden; padding: 0px 16px; height: 48px;"><div style="font-size: 12px;">Use code with caution.</div><svg fill="currentColor" height="18px" viewBox="0 -960 960 960" width="18px"><path d="M360-240q-33 0-56.5-23.5T280-320v-480q0-33 23.5-56.5T360-880h360q33 0 56.5 23.5T800-800v480q0 33-23.5 56.5T720-240H360Zm0-80h360v-480H360v480ZM200-80q-33 0-56.5-23.5T120-160v-560h80v560h440v80H200Zm160-240v-480 480Z"></path></svg></div></div></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Performance</span>: While compilation works, it is significantly slower than on a native machine. In 2011, users reported it being roughly&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">140x slower</span>&nbsp;than native execution.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Modern Versions</span>: Today's versions of&nbsp;<span><a rel="noopener" href="https://bellard.org/jslinux/" style="text-decoration-thickness: 1px; text-decoration-color: var(--JKqx2); -webkit-tap-highlight-color: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.1); text-underline-offset: 1px; outline: 0px;">JSLinux</a></span>&nbsp;(which use WebAssembly) often include full&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">GNU toolchains</span>&nbsp;in their Fedora or Alpine Linux distributions, allowing for more complex builds, including assembly language and larger C projects.</span><span><span style="white-space: nowrap; The&nbsp;<span><a rel="noopener" href="https://bellard.org/jslinux/tech.html" style="text-decoration-thickness: 1px; text-decoration-color: var(--JKqx2); -webkit-tap-highlight-color: rgba(255, 255, Think of JSLinux as the "motherboard and CPU" and the Linux kernel as the "software" plugged into it.<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">1. font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">The Linux kernel is indeed large, but JSLinux uses a&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">compressed kernel image</span>&nbsp;(typically a&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">vmlinuz</code>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">bzImage</code>&nbsp;file).<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">The Transfer:</span>&nbsp;When you open the webpage, the browser downloads the kernel image (usually ~2–5MB) and a disk image (the filesystem) via standard HTTP requests.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">The RAM:</span>&nbsp;JSLinux allocates a large JavaScript&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">TypedArray</code>&nbsp;(like&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">Uint8Array</code>) to act as the "Physical RAM." It "pokes" the kernel bytes into the start of this array and tells the emulated CPU to start executing at that memory address.</span><span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">2. Is TCC in JS?<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);"><span style="font-weight: 700;">No.</span>&nbsp;This is the "magic" of emulation.<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">TCC is a standard Linux binary</span>&nbsp;compiled for x86. It is stored inside the disk image.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">When you type&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">tcc</code>&nbsp;in the terminal, the Linux kernel (running inside the emulator) loads that x86 binary into the emulated RAM.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">The JSLinux "CPU" then reads those x86 instructions one by one, translates them into JavaScript logic, and executes them.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">JSLinux doesn't need to know what TCC is.</span>&nbsp;As long as the emulator can correctly execute the x86 instruction set,&nbsp;<em style="font-weight: inherit;">any</em>&nbsp;program compiled for that architecture will run.</span><span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">3. Does it "Explicitly Support" the Compiler?<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);"><span style="font-weight: 700;">No.</span>&nbsp;JSLinux doesn't have a single line of code dedicated to "supporting" TCC,&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">ls</code>, or&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">vi</code>.<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">It only supports the&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">x86 CPU instructions</span>&nbsp;and a few basic hardware devices (like a serial port for text and a timer).</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">Because the Linux kernel only talks to the CPU and those specific devices, it "thinks" it's on a real computer.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">Everything else (compiling, file management, shell scripts) happens purely within the&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">emulated environment</span>&nbsp;using standard Linux files.</span><span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">4. How it Handles the "Large" Filesystem<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">Since a full Linux OS is hundreds of megabytes, JSLinux uses a&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">Copy-on-Write (COW)</span>&nbsp;system or fetches blocks on demand.<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">It doesn't download the whole 1GB disk image at once.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">It downloads a small "boot" portion, and as the OS asks for more files (like the C compiler), the emulator fetches those specific "blocks" of data from the server.</span><span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></li></ul><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">Would you like to see how the&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">memory mapping</span>&nbsp;(the&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">TypedArray</code>&nbsp;trick) looks in the source code?<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div></div><div><div style="clear: both; display: flex; flex-flow: wrap; row-gap: 16px; margin-block: 18px 0px; justify-content: space-between;"><div style="display: contents;"></div><div style="display: flex; gap: 4px; flex-shrink: 1; width: 652px; align-items: center;"><div style="display: flex;"><div style="position: relative; display: inline-flex;"><span style="inline-size: 20px; block-size: 20px;"><div><svg fill="currentColor" width="20px" height="20px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 -1 13 18"><path d="M1.77734 2.96289C2.10462 2.96289 2.37012 3.22838 2.37012 3.55566C2.37003 3.86235 2.13657 4.11509 1.83789 4.14551L1.7168 4.15137C1.41824 4.18181 1.18479 4.43369 1.18457 4.74023V13.0361C1.18467 14.0181 1.98137 14.8145 2.96289 14.8145H8.88867C9.19535 14.8145 9.44797 14.5818 9.47852 14.2832L9.48438 14.1611C9.51492 13.8625 9.76754 13.6299 10.0742 13.6299C10.4012 13.63 10.6658 13.8947 10.666 14.2217C10.666 15.2035 9.87051 16 8.88867 16H2.96289C1.3263 16 0.000103459 14.6722 0 13.0361V4.74023C0.000234322 3.75868 0.795773 2.96304 1.77734 2.96289ZM12.4443 2.37012C12.4442 1.71576 11.9141 1.18568 11.2598 1.18555H5.33398L5.21289 1.19141C4.65505 1.24796 4.21101 1.69123 4.1543 2.24902L4.14844 2.37012V11.2588C4.14844 11.5656 4.38192 11.8182 4.68066 11.8486L4.74121 11.8516H11.2598C11.9141 11.8514 12.4442 11.3213 12.4443 10.667V2.37012ZM13.6299 10.667C13.6297 11.9759 12.5687 13.037 11.2598 13.0371H4.74121C3.75937 13.0371 2.96289 12.2406 2.96289 11.2588V2.37012C2.96303 1.06111 4.02495 2.48186e-07 5.33398 0H11.2598C12.5687 0.000137107 13.6297 1.0612 13.6299 2.37012V10.667Z"></path></svg></div></span></div></div><div><div><div style="display: flex; inline-size: 44px;"><div style="inline-size: 20px; block-size: 20px;"><svg fill="currentColor" width="20px" height="20px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="3 3 18 18"><path d="M15.9229 contents;"></div></div><div style="display: flex; flex-direction: column; width: 652.438px;"><div style="display: contents;"></div></div></div><div><div style="padding-bottom: 12px; min-height: 100%; margin-top: var(--rhYkpc--F7qGTe,-80px); width: var(--rhYkpc--MPtIS,372px); padding-inline-start: var(--rhYkpc--jCcM0d,76px);"><div style="display: contents;"></div></div></div><div></div><div></div></div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div></div></div></div><div style="--fade-in-animation: fade-in-new-response 150ms cubic-bezier(0.3,0,0.8,0.15); animation: var(--fade-in-animation); padding-top: 30px; position: relative; margin-top: 24px;"><div style="position: relative; padding-bottom: 10px; max-width: 652px; z-index: 1; margin-top: 0px;"><div><div style="display: flex; gap: 4px; margin-left: auto; width: fit-content;"><div style="display: flex; position: relative; overflow: hidden; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 24px 4px 24px 24px; padding: 12px 16px; width: fit-content; flex-direction: column; max-inline-size: 472px; margin-left: auto;"><div style="display: flex; flex-direction: row;"><span role="heading" style="-webkit-box-orient: vertical; -webkit-line-clamp: 2; display: -webkit-box; overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; overflow-wrap: break-word; font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 16px; line-height: 24px;">what? the kernel only takes 5mb? what is it. file type. how could js run that in 2011?</span></div></div></div><div style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: flex; font-size: 12px; justify-content: end; line-height: 16px;"></div><div></div></div></div><div><div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div></div><div></div><div><div><div style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--m3c11,#eef0ff); position: relative; --m3c9: #e6e8f0; --m3c11: #e6e8f0; display: flex;"><div style="width: 652.438px;"><div><div style="display: contents;"></div></div><div dir="ltr" style="width: 652px; max-width: var(--CYi3c--fRcLaf,652px);"><div style="display: contents;"><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);"><div style="display: contents;">The Linux kernel is remarkably flexible; while a standard desktop kernel can be over 100MB, a highly stripped-down version for embedded systems can be as small as&nbsp;</div><span style="font-weight: 700;">1MB to 5MB</span>.<span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 64.3359px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">Reddit</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+3</span></span></div></span></span></div><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">1. What is the "Kernel File"?<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">The file used in JSLinux (often named&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">vmlinux26.bin</code>) is a&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">raw binary image</span>&nbsp;of the compiled kernel.<span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 94.3828px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">Stack Overflow</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;"></span></span></div></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Minimalist Config:</span>&nbsp;Fabrice Bellard used a custom configuration (<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">make allnoconfig</code>) that stripped out everything not strictly necessary for his emulator, such as graphics drivers, sound, and complex networking.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Specific Architecture:</span>&nbsp;It was compiled for a basic&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">32-bit x86</span>&nbsp;target (roughly an Intel 486).</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">The "bzImage" Format:</span>&nbsp;Typically, kernels are stored as a&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">bzImage</code>&nbsp;(big zImage), which is a self-extracting compressed file. When JSLinux "boots," it loads this compressed binary into memory, and the kernel's own internal code decompresses it into the emulated RAM.</span><span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 109.875px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">Stack Overflow</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+4</span></span></div></span></span></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">2. How did JS run it in 2011?<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">In 2011, JavaScript engines (like V8 in Chrome and SpiderMonkey in Firefox) had just become fast enough to handle this through three key innovations:<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Typed Arrays:</span>&nbsp;This was the "secret sauce". Before Typed Arrays (like&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">Uint8Array</code>), JavaScript handled numbers as 64-bit floats, which was too slow and memory-intensive for emulation. Typed Arrays allowed Bellard to allocate a large, contiguous block of&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">raw binary memory</span>&nbsp;that behaved exactly like physical RAM.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">The Opcode Loop:</span>&nbsp;Bellard wrote a massive "switch" statement or look-up table in JavaScript. For every byte in the kernel's binary, the JS would say: "This byte is a&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">0x89</code>&nbsp;opcode; that means&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">MOV</code>. I will now update my&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">registers</code>&nbsp;object to reflect that move".</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Just-In-Time (JIT) Compilation:</span>&nbsp;2011 was the era when browsers started compiling JS into machine code on the fly. This made the emulator's execution loop fast enough to feel "real-time," even though it was technically "software" (JS) running "software" (Linux).</span><span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 75.0312px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">YouTube</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+4</span></span></div></span></span></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">3. Does it need code for the compiler?<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">No. JSLinux provides the&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">hardware</span>&nbsp;(CPU, RAM, Interrupts). The kernel provides the&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">environment</span>&nbsp;(File system, Process management). The compiler (TCC) is just an x86 program sitting on the "disk" image. When you run it, the JSLinux CPU executes the compiler's x86 instructions exactly like it executed the kernel's.<span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 104.93px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); height: fit-content; margin-left: 8px; margin-top: auto; display: flex; flex: 1 1 auto; place-content: end; outline: 0px;"><div style="color: rgb(139, 140, 145); height: 14px; margin-bottom: 2px; rotate: 180deg; max-width: var(--CYi3c--fRcLaf,652px);"><div style="display: contents;"><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);"><div style="display: contents;">It is a&nbsp;</div><span style="font-weight: 700;">raw binary image</span>, but not in the way a video or image file is parsed. It contains&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">actual x86 machine code</span>&nbsp;(CPU instructions) that the JavaScript emulator executes one by one.<span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">1. It's Not a DSL<span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">JSLinux does&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">not</span>&nbsp;parse the kernel as a string or a custom domain-specific language (DSL). Instead, it treats the kernel file as a long sequence of bytes.<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">The Loading Process</span>: The browser downloads the kernel (e.g.,&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">vmlinux26.bin</code>) and copies those bytes into a large&nbsp;<span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">JavaScript TypedArray</span>&nbsp;(specifically a&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">Uint8Array</code>) which acts as the emulated computer's RAM.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">The Execution</span>: The emulator points its "instruction pointer" to the first byte of that array and enters a loop.</span><span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 63.0391px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">Quora</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+2</span></span></div></span></span></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">2. How JavaScript "Runs" Binary<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">In the 2011 version, the emulator works through a massive&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">interpreter loop</span>. It doesn't "understand" Linux; it only understands the x86 processor instructions.<span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><ol style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 20px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: decimal;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Fetch</span>: It reads the byte at the current memory address (e.g.,&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">0x89</code>).</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: decimal;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Decode</span>: It uses a large&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">switch</code>&nbsp;statement or an array of functions where the index is the byte value.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: decimal;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Execute</span>: If it sees&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">0x89</code>, the JavaScript code performs the logic for an x86&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">MOV</code>&nbsp;instruction (moving data between virtual registers or memory).</span><span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 109.125px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">Stack Overflow</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+2</span></span></div></span></span></li></ol><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">3. Why the Kernel is "Small" (5MB)<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">The 5MB file is a&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">stripped vmlinux binary</span>.<span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 109.039px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">Gentoo Forums</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+1</span></span></div></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">No Overhead</span>: Most "large" kernels include drivers for thousands of real-world devices (WiFi, GPUs, Printers). Fabrice Bellard compiled a custom kernel that&nbsp;<em style="font-weight: inherit;">only</em>&nbsp;includes drivers for the few simple, virtual devices his JavaScript code emulates.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Raw Code</span>: All debugging information (symbols like function names) is "stripped" out, leaving only the bare machine code instructions that the CPU needs to run.</span><span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 109.039px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">Gentoo Forums</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+1</span></span></div></span></span></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">4. Why JavaScript was fast enough in 2011<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">This only worked because of&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">JIT (Just-In-Time) compilation</span>&nbsp;in modern browsers. The browser's engine (like Chrome's V8) sees the repetitive JavaScript execution loop and compiles&nbsp;<em style="font-weight: inherit;">that</em>&nbsp;into native machine code on your real computer. Essentially, you have your real CPU running highly optimized browser code, which in turn simulates the logic of a virtual x86 CPU.<span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 64.1562px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">Reddit</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+2</span></span></div></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); Each byte represents a specific action for the CPU.</div><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">1. In x86, these are variable-length.
