min-width: 4em; vertical-align: top; color: var(--bbQxAb); font-family: var(--LI4Bo); font-size: var(--Mhs7de); font-weight: var(--ofwUBc); line-height: var(--XWv1if); letter-spacing: 0px; padding: 12px 0px;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Execute</span>&nbsp;a sub-routine (like a function).</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">2. How JavaScript "Iterates Forward"</div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">The JSLinux emulator works by running a&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">Fetch-Decode-Execute</span>&nbsp;loop. It doesn't read the whole file like a book; it acts as a pointer moving through an array of these bytes.</div><ol style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 20px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: decimal;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Fetch</span>: JavaScript looks at the current index in the "RAM" array (the&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">Instruction Pointer</code>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">EIP</code>).</span><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: decimal; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><em style="font-weight: inherit;">JS Code:</em>&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">let opcode = RAM[EIP];</code></span></li></ul></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: decimal;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Decode</span>: It uses a massive&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">switch</code>&nbsp;statement or a lookup table to decide what that byte means.</span><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: decimal; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><em style="font-weight: inherit;">JS Code:</em>&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">switch(opcode) { case 0xB8: ... }</code></span></li></ul></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: decimal;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Execute</span>: It performs the JavaScript logic that simulates the CPU's reaction.</span><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: decimal; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><em style="font-weight: inherit;">Example:</em>&nbsp;If the byte is&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">0xB8</code>&nbsp;(the first byte of a "Move to EAX" command), the JS code will:</span><ol style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 20px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: decimal; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">Read the next 4 bytes (the value to move).</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: decimal; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">Store that value in a&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">Int32Array</code>&nbsp;representing the CPU's registers.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: decimal; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">Increment the&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">EIP</code>&nbsp;index so it points to the next command.</span></li></ol></li></ul></li></ol><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">3. Handling the "Large" Kernel</div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">The kernel isn't run as one single "loop." It is a massive web of jumps and branches.</div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Linear Execution</span>: It runs forward byte-by-byte for basic tasks (like setting up memory).</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Non-Linear Jumps</span>: When the code reaches a "Jump" (<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">0xEB</code>) or "Call" (<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">0xE8</code>), the emulator simply changes its&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">EIP</code>&nbsp;index to a new location in the array. This allows the 5MB kernel to "loop" and "jump" across millions of instructions while the JavaScript simply keeps following the pointer.</span></li></ul><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">In essence, JSLinux is a&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">translator</span>. It reads "x86 language" (bytes) and speaks "JavaScript actions" (updating array values).</div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">Would you like to see the&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">minimal C code</span>&nbsp;that generates one of these tiny binary files?</div><div></div><div><div style="clear: both; display: flex; flex-flow: wrap; row-gap: 16px; margin-block: 18px 0px; justify-content: space-between;"><div style="display: contents;"></div><div style="display: flex; gap: 4px; flex-shrink: 1; width: 652px; align-items: center;"><div style="display: flex;"><div style="position: relative; display: inline-flex;"><span style="inline-size: 20px; block-size: 20px;"><div><svg fill="currentColor" width="20px" height="20px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" No Semicolons: Variable-Length Opcodes<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">In x86, there are&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">no separators</span>&nbsp;or semicolons. The CPU (and JSLinux) knows when an instruction ends based on the&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">Opcode</span>&nbsp;(the first byte).<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">Think of it like a language where the first letter tells you how many letters follow:<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">If the first "letter" is&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;"><code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">A</code></span>, the rules say "A is always 1 byte long."</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">If the first "letter" is&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;"><code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">B</code></span>, the rules say "B always takes the next 4 bytes as data."</span><span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></li></ul><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Example in x86 bytes:</span><br><code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">90 B8 01 00 00 00</code><span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><ol style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 20px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: decimal;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">The emulator reads&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">90</code>. It looks up&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">90</code>&nbsp;in its table and sees it's&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">NOP</code>&nbsp;(No Operation). It's a&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">1-byte</span>&nbsp;instruction.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: decimal;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">The emulator moves the pointer (+1) to&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">B8</code>.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: decimal;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">It looks up&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">B8</code>. The table says: "This is&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">MOV EAX</code>, and it&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">must</span>&nbsp;be followed by 4 bytes of data."</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: decimal;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">The emulator automatically grabs the next 4 bytes (<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">01 00 00 00</code>) as the value.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: decimal;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">It moves the pointer (+5 total) to the next instruction.</span><span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></li></ol><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">If the emulator or the kernel gets&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">one single byte off</span>, the whole system crashes because it starts "reading the data as instructions."<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">2. Can Linux "Just Work" this way?<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Yes.</span>&nbsp;If you perfectly emulate the ~200-300 most common x86 instructions and a few hardware "ports" (like a way to print text to a screen), the Linux kernel will run.<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">The kernel is just a massive collection of these instructions. It manages things like:<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Memory:</span>&nbsp;"Keep track of which bytes in the TypedArray are used by which program."</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Scheduling:</span>&nbsp;"Run Program A for 10ms (by jumping the pointer), then jump the pointer to Program B."</span><span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">3. Is the Kernel an Infinite Loop?<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Effectively, yes.</span><br>When Linux boots, it runs a "setup" sequence (linear instructions). Once it's finished booting, it enters the&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">Idle Loop</span>.<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">The CPU stays in a loop waiting for an&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">Interrupt</span>&nbsp;(like you typing a key or a timer ticking).</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">When you type a key, the JavaScript emulator "injects" an interrupt.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">The CPU pointer "jumps" to the keyboard-handling code in the kernel, processes your key, and then jumps back to the loop.</span><span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">4. The "Assembly" Connection<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">Assembly is just the&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">human-readable version</span>&nbsp;of those hex bytes.<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Assembly:</span>&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">mov eax, 1</code></span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Machine Code (Hex):</span>&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">B8 01 00 00 00</code></span><span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></li></ul><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">JSLinux reads the&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">Hex</span>, but it performs the logic defined by the&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">Assembly</span>.<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">Would you like to see the&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">JavaScript&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">switch</code>&nbsp;case</span>&nbsp;that actually handles one of these "multi-byte" instructions?<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: style="position: relative; padding-bottom: 10px; max-width: 652px; z-index: 1; margin-top: 0px;"><div><div style="display: flex; gap: 4px; margin-left: auto; width: fit-content;"><div style="display: the methods are not really hard to implement, esp when you live on a higher level environment like js where lots of language features are available.</span><div role="button" tabindex="0" style="align-items: center; height: fit-content; margin-left: 8px; margin-top: auto; display: flex; flex: 1 1 auto; place-content: end; outline: 0px;"><div style="color: rgb(139, 140, 145); height: sans-serif; color: var(--m3c11,#eef0ff); position: relative; --m3c9: #e6e8f0; --m3c11: #e6e8f0; display: flex;"><div style="width: 652.438px;"><div><div style="display: contents;"></div></div><div dir="ltr" style="width: 652px; max-width: var(--CYi3c--fRcLaf,652px);"><div style="display: contents;"><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);"><div style="display: contents;">Exactly. You've nailed the "why." Because Fabrice Bellard wrote this in&nbsp;</div><span style="font-weight: 700;">JavaScript</span>, he could offload a massive amount of the heavy lifting to the browser's engine, which a C programmer writing a "real" emulator would have to do manually.<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">Here is why the high-level nature of JS makes the code so compact:<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">1. The "TypedArray" is the Hardware<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">In C, managing memory involves complex pointers and manual buffer management. In JS, one line:<br><code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">var ram = new Uint8Array(32 * 1024 * 1024);</code><br>...instantly creates&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">32MB of "physical RAM"</span>&nbsp;that the browser's garbage collector and memory manager handle for you. The emulator just reads and writes to indices in that array.<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">2. Offloading Complex Logic<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">The Scheduler:</span>&nbsp;JSLinux doesn't need a complex timing system to "yield" to the OS. It uses&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">setTimeout</code>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">requestAnimationFrame</code>. This allows the browser to handle the "wait" states while the emulator is idle.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">The Console:</span>&nbsp;Instead of writing a VGA driver or a pixel-perfect terminal renderer from scratch, Bellard just mapped the serial output of the kernel to a simple&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">HTML&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">&lt;textarea&gt;</code></span>&nbsp;or a pre-made JS terminal library.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Math:</span>&nbsp;x86 math (like 64-bit operations) is "hard" in assembly but "one-liners" in JS. Modern JS engines handle overflows and bitwise logic very efficiently.</span><span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">3. The "Instruction Table" is a JS Object<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">Instead of a complex linked list or binary tree to find instructions, he could use a simple&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">JavaScript array of functions</span>.<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div></div><div style="margin-block: 24px 32px; color: var(--jINu6c);"><div><div style="background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 16px 16px 4px 4px; overflow: auto hidden; padding: 12px 16px 0px;"><div style="display: flex; justify-content: space-between;"><div style="font-family: var(--Eou8Yc); font-size: var(--GiToJf); line-height: var(--qWZYEc); letter-spacing: 0px;">javascript</div></div><div dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; overflow-x: auto;"><pre><code><span style="color: rgb(154, 160, 166); font-style: italic;">// A simplified look at how the 'table' might look</span><span>
</span><span style="color: rgb(197, 138, 249);">var</span><span> opcodes = [];
opcodes[</span><span style="color: rgb(250, 144, 62);">0x90</span><span>] = </span><span style="color: rgb(197, 138, 249);">function</span><span>() { </span><span style="color: rgb(154, 160, 166); font-style: italic;">/* NOP: do nothing */</span><span> };
opcodes[</span><span style="color: rgb(250, 144, 62);">0xB8</span><span>] = </span><span style="color: rgb(197, 138, 249);">function</span><span>() { 
    cpu.eax = read_32_bits(); </span><span style="color: rgb(154, 160, 166); font-style: italic;">// JS handles the bit-shifting logic</span><span>
};

</span><span style="color: rgb(154, 160, 166); font-style: italic;">// The main loop is then just:</span><span>
</span><span style="color: rgb(197, 138, 249);">while</span><span>(running) {
    opcodes[ram[eip]](); </span><span style="color: rgb(154, 160, 166); font-style: italic;">// Execute the function at that hex index</span><span>
}
</span></code></pre></div></div><div style="display: flex; justify-content: space-between; align-items: center; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px 4px 16px 16px; margin-top: 3px; overflow: hidden; padding: 0px 16px; height: 48px;"><div style="font-size: 12px;">Use code with caution.</div><svg fill="currentColor" height="18px" viewBox="0 -960 960 960" width="18px"><path d="M360-240q-33 0-56.5-23.5T280-320v-480q0-33 23.5-56.5T360-880h360q33 0 56.5 23.5T800-800v480q0 33-23.5 56.5T720-240H360Zm0-80h360v-480H360v480ZM200-80q-33 0-56.5-23.5T120-160v-560h80v560h440v80H200Zm160-240v-480 480Z"></path></svg></div></div></div><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">4. The "Minimalist" Strategy<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">Bellard is famous for knowing exactly what to&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">exclude</span>. By excluding support for things like USB, Sound, 3D Graphics, and legacy Floppy Disk controllers, he reduced the "surface area" of the computer to the bare essentials needed for a Linux terminal.<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">It’s less of a "full PC" and more of a&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">"C-to-Hardware translator"</span>&nbsp;that only translates the vocabulary Linux actually speaks.<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">Would you like to see a comparison of an&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">x86 Instruction</span>&nbsp;in assembly vs the&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">JavaScript code</span>&nbsp;that simulates it?<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div></div><div><div style="clear: both; display: flex; flex-flow: wrap; row-gap: 16px; margin-block: 18px 0px; justify-content: space-between;"><div style="display: contents;"></div><div style="display: flex; gap: 4px; flex-shrink: 1; width: 652px; align-items: center;"><div style="display: flex;"><div style="position: relative; display: inline-flex;"><span style="inline-size: 20px; block-size: 20px;"><div><svg fill="currentColor" width="20px" height="20px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 -1 13 18"><path d="M1.77734 2.96289C2.10462 2.96289 2.37012 3.22838 2.37012 3.55566C2.37003 3.86235 2.13657 4.11509 1.83789 4.14551L1.7168 4.15137C1.41824 contents;"></div></div></div><div></div><div></div></div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div></div></div></div><div flex; position: relative; overflow: hidden; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 24px 4px 24px 24px; padding: 12px 16px; width: fit-content; flex-direction: column; max-inline-size: 472px; assembly</span></div></div></div><div style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: flex; font-size: 12px; justify-content: end; line-height: 16px;"></div><div></div></div></div><div><div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div></div><div></div><div><div><div style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--m3c11,#eef0ff); position: relative; --m3c9: #e6e8f0; --m3c11: #e6e8f0; display: flex;"><div style="width: 652.438px;"><div><div style="display: contents;"></div></div><div dir="ltr" style="width: 652px; max-width: var(--CYi3c--fRcLaf,652px);"><div style="display: contents;"><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);"><mark style="border-radius: 4px; background-image: ; background-position-x: ; background-position-y: ; background-size: ; background-repeat: ; background-attachment: ; background-origin: ; background-clip: ; padding: 0px 2px;"><div style="display: contents;">There is&nbsp;</div><span style="font-weight: 700;">no single universal standard</span>&nbsp;for assembly language</mark>. Unlike higher-level languages like C or Python, which have formal international standards (like ISO), assembly is specific to the&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">CPU architecture</span>&nbsp;and the&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">Assembler</span>&nbsp;program you use.<span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 109.125px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">Stack Overflow</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+2</span></span></div></span></span></div><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">1. The Two Main Syntaxes (Flavors)<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">Even for the exact same x86 processor, there are two primary ways to write the code:<span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 107.766px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; letter-spacing: 0px; padding: 8px 16px 8px 0px; text-align: left;">Feature<span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; The "De Facto" Standards<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">While there isn't a formal committee standard, developers follow these "authorities":<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Manufacturer Manuals:</span>&nbsp;The ultimate reference for what the CPU can do is the&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><div style="display: inline;"><a tabindex="0" role="button" href="https://www.google.com/search?q=intel+sdm+%28software+developer%E2%80%99s+manual%29&amp;kgmid=%2Fhkb%2F1717470280&amp;sa=X&amp;ved=2ahUKEwib9qW138-TAxX9LEQIHYxrJ_kQ3egRegYIAQgJEAI&amp;gl=us" style="text-decoration-thickness: 10%; text-decoration-style: dotted; text-decoration-color: rgb(139, 140, 145); -webkit-tap-highlight-color: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.1); text-underline-offset: 12%; outline: 0px;">Intel SDM (Software Developer’s Manual)</a></div></span></span>&nbsp;or the&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><div style="display: inline;"><a tabindex="0" role="button" href="https://www.google.com/search?q=amd64+architecture+programmer%27s+manual&amp;kgmid=%2Fhkb%2F-922571967&amp;sa=X&amp;ved=2ahUKEwib9qW138-TAxX9LEQIHYxrJ_kQ3egRegYIAQgJEAQ&amp;gl=us" style="text-decoration-thickness: 10%; text-decoration-style: dotted; text-decoration-color: rgb(139, 140, 145); -webkit-tap-highlight-color: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.1); text-underline-offset: 12%; outline: 0px;">AMD64 Architecture Programmer's Manual</a></div></span></span>. These define the opcodes (hex bytes) and the intended behavior.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Assembler-Specific Rules:</span>&nbsp;Different programs (Assemblers) have their own "dialects" for things like macros and data definitions:</span><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: circle; padding-inline-start: 0px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">NASM</span>&nbsp;/&nbsp;<span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">YASM</span>:</span>&nbsp;Popular open-source assemblers that use a clean version of Intel syntax.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: circle; padding-inline-start: 0px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">MASM</span>:</span>&nbsp;Microsoft's assembler, used for Windows development.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: circle; padding-inline-start: 0px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">GAS (GNU Assembler)</span>:</span>&nbsp;The default for Linux (GCC), which historically uses AT&amp;T syntax but can support Intel via a directive.</span><span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 64.4531px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">Reddit</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+6</span></span></div></span></span></li></ul></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">3. The Instruction Set Architecture (ISA)<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">The only "hard" standard is the&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">Instruction Set Architecture (ISA)</span>. This is the contract between the hardware and the software. It defines:<span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 107.766px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">Stack Overflow</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+1</span></span></div></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">The exact&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">binary encoding</span>&nbsp;of every instruction (the hex bytes JSLinux reads).</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">The&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">Register Set</span>&nbsp;(like&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">EAX</code>,&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">EBX</code>,&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">RSP</code>).</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">The&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">Memory Model</span>&nbsp;(how addresses are calculated).</span><span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 109.875px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">Stack Overflow</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+4</span></span></div></span></span></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">4. Failed Standardization Efforts<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">The IEEE did attempt to create a universal standard (<span style="font-weight: 700;">IEEE 694-1985</span>) to unify assembly syntax across different chips. However, it was&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">largely ignored</span>&nbsp;by the industry and has since been withdrawn, as chip manufacturers and tool developers preferred their own established conventions.<span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 94.3828px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">Stack Overflow</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;"></span></span></div></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">Would you like to see how a&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">specific C function</span>&nbsp;translates into both Intel and AT&amp;T assembly styles?<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div></div><div><div style="clear: both; display: flex; flex-flow: wrap; row-gap: 16px; margin-block: 18px 0px; justify-content: AMD (The "Compatible" Extension)<span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">The Assembly</span>: You still have to choose between&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">Intel Syntax</span>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">AT&amp;T Syntax</span>&nbsp;depending on your compiler. AMD and Intel are "binary compatible," meaning they speak the same machine language but don't care how you style your text files.</span><span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">2. ARM (The "Licensed" Standard)<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">ARM is different because one company,&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">ARM Holdings</span>, owns the design.<span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 65.8984px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">Wikipedia</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;"></span></span></div></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">The Standard</span>: ARM publishes an official&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">Architecture Reference Manual</span>. Because they license the design to others (like Apple or Samsung), there is a much stronger "official" way to write ARM assembly compared to the x86 chaos.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Variations</span>: However, different tools (like&nbsp;<span><a rel="noopener" href="https://www.arm.com/" style="text-decoration-thickness: 1px; text-decoration-color: var(--JKqx2); -webkit-tap-highlight-color: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.1); text-underline-offset: 1px; outline: 0px;">Keil</a></span>&nbsp;vs.&nbsp;<span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">GNU Assembler</span>) still use slightly different directives for things like macros or defining data.</span><span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 81.3906px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">Wikipedia</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+4</span></span></div></span></span></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">3. RISC-V (The "Open" Standard)<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">RISC-V is the closest thing to an "open-source" ISA.<span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 79.2812px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">Wikipedia</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+1</span></span></div></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">The Standard</span>: It is managed by&nbsp;<span><a rel="noopener" href="https://riscv.org/" style="text-decoration-thickness: 1px; text-decoration-color: var(--JKqx2); -webkit-tap-highlight-color: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.1); text-underline-offset: 1px; outline: 0px;">RISC-V International</a></span>, a non-profit. They define the exact binary opcodes and a&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">recommended assembly syntax</span>&nbsp;to keep the ecosystem from fragmenting.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">The Goal</span>: They want a program compiled for one RISC-V chip to run on any other RISC-V chip without modification.</span><span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 64.9062px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">Reddit</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+4</span></span></div></span></span></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">Summary of "Standards"<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div></div><div style="overflow-x: auto; margin-block: 16px 24px; box-sizing: border-box; scrollbar-width: none; inline-size: calc(100% + 20px); padding-inline-end: 24px;"><table style="border: none; border-collapse: collapse; table-layout: auto; width: 648px;"><tbody><tr><th colspan="undefined" style="border-bottom: 1px solid var(--gS5jXb); min-width: 4em; vertical-align: top; font-family: var(--LI4Bo); font-size: var(--Mhs7de); line-height: var(--XWv1if); letter-spacing: 0px; padding: 8px 16px 8px 0px; text-align: left;">Name<span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; AMD (Cross-licensed)</td><td colspan="undefined" style="border-bottom: 1px solid var(--gS5jXb); min-width: 4em; vertical-align: top; color: var(--bbQxAb); font-family: var(--LI4Bo); font-size: var(--Mhs7de); min-width: 4em; vertical-align: top; color: var(--bbQxAb); font-family: var(--LI4Bo); font-size: var(--Mhs7de); font-weight: var(--ofwUBc); line-height: var(--XWv1if); letter-spacing: 0px; padding: 12px 16px 12px 0px;">RISC-V International (Open)</td><td colspan="undefined" style="border-bottom: none; min-width: 4em; vertical-align: top; color: var(--bbQxAb); font-family: var(--LI4Bo); font-size: var(--Mhs7de); font-weight: var(--ofwUBc); line-height: var(--XWv1if); letter-spacing: 0px; padding: 12px 0px;">Unified (By Design)</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">The&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">ISA</span>&nbsp;is the rulebook for the hardware (the hex bytes JSLinux reads). The&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">Assembly Language</span>&nbsp;is just the "human skin" we put over those bytes so we don't have to type&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">B8 01 00</code>&nbsp;manually.<span><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 64.1562px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">Reddit</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+2</span></span></div></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); supports&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">RISC-V</span>&nbsp;now, would you like to see how a RISC-V "Add" instruction looks in its modern&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">WebAssembly</span>-based core?<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="white-space: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; width: 14px;"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" height="14px" viewBox="0 0 12 7" width="14px" fill="none"><path d="M6.00046 0.166733C5.88929 0.166733 5.78654 0.184733 5.69221 0.220733C5.59771 0.256899 5.50604 0.3194 5.41721 0.408234L0.583711 5.24173C0.422711 5.40273 0.340795 5.59573 0.337962 5.82073C0.335128 6.04573 0.417045 6.24157 0.583711 6.40823C0.744878 6.5694 0.939379 6.64998 1.16721 6.64998C1.39488 6.64998 1.5893 6.5694 1.75046 6.40823L6.00046 2.16673L10.2505 6.40823C10.4116 6.5694 10.6047 6.6514 10.8297 6.65423C11.0547 6.6569 11.2505 6.5749 11.4172 6.40823C11.5782 6.24723 11.6587 6.05282 11.6587 5.82498C11.6587 5.59715 11.5782 5.40273 11.4172 5.24173L6.58371 0.408234C6.49488 0.3194 6.40321 0.256899 6.30871 0.220733C6.21438 0.184733 6.11163 0.166733 6.00046 0.166733Z" fill="currentColor"></path></svg></div></div></div></div></div><div style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: flex; font-size: 12px; justify-content: end; line-height: 16px;"></div><div></div></div></div><div></div><div><div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div></div><div></div><div><div><div style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif;
