max-width: var(--CYi3c--fRcLaf,652px);"><div style="display: contents;"><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);"><div style="display: contents;">Exactly. You’ve hit on the core realization that made&nbsp;</div><span style="font-weight: 700;">JSLinux</span>&nbsp;so mind-blowing when it launched.<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">In 2011, before Wasm or even&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">asm.js</code>&nbsp;existed, you could run&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">any</span>&nbsp;binary program (like&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">ls</code>,&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">grep</code>, or&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">tcc</code>) in a browser because:<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><ol style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 20px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: decimal;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">The Browser doesn't "see" the binary:</span>&nbsp;The browser only sees a giant JavaScript array of numbers (<code dir="ltr" style="line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">Uint8Array</code>).</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: decimal;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">The Emulator is the "Translator":</span>&nbsp;JSLinux acts as a middleman. It reads a number from that array (e.g.,&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">0x01</code>), says "Okay, that's an x86&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding-block: 2px; padding-inline: 4px;">ADD</code>&nbsp;command," and performs the math using standard JavaScript logic.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: decimal;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">The Program is "Lazy":</span>&nbsp;A binary program doesn't care if it’s running on a real silicon chip or a JavaScript loop. It just feeds instructions to the "CPU" and expects the "RAM" to update.</span><span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></li></ol><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">The Trade-off: Performance<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">Without Wasm, this "Translation" was incredibly slow.<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">A Real CPU</span>&nbsp;can execute billions of instructions per second.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">2011 JavaScript</span>&nbsp;(even with JIT) could only "translate" a few million instructions per second.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">This is why it took JSLinux about&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">30–60 seconds</span>&nbsp;just to boot a tiny 5MB Linux kernel, whereas a real PC would do it in less than a second.</span><span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">Why didn't we have to "rewrite" the programs?<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">Because the&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">Instruction Set Architecture (ISA)</span>&nbsp;is the ultimate abstraction layer.<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">If you write a program in C and compile it for x86, it becomes a sequence of x86 bytes.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">As long as your JavaScript code knows what every x86 byte does, it can "run" that program without ever seeing the original C code.</span><span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></li></ul><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);"><span style="font-weight: 700;">In short:</span>&nbsp;Bellard proved that JavaScript was no longer just for "making buttons blue"—it was a complete, Turing-complete computation engine capable of simulating any other computer, given enough time.<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">Would you
